text:
This is one of the best muffin recipes I've ever tried.  I say best because I've often had difficulty baking muffins that actually puff up tall in the pans when baking, and this definitely makes delicious, springy, moist muffins.

I agree with a few posters that some additional liquid can be used, which was my method for baking.  However, I don't think this takes away from the recipe because it may have to do with the freshness of the peaches used.  Very ripe fresh peaches would not require as much liquid to make a substantial batter.
I have also tried baking the recipe as a loaf, and that came out equally as good.

I also think this is a very solid recipe that is open to changes - some cranberries or nuts would make nice additions.  But on its own, it's wonderful.  I highly recommend it.

text:
These are very good muffins.  I followed other users' advice and added a half cup of milk to the batter, which helped.  The first time I made these they burned around the edges, so the next time I used paper baking cups to line the pans and cooked them for just 20 minutes; they turned out perfect.  I definitely recommend using fresh peaches rather than canned.  These muffins have a great texture and aren't too sweet.  Thanks for sharing!

text:
I cut this recipe in half. Because I didn't want to use half of an egg, I used both eggs and cut out the extra two tablespoons of vegetable oil. As with all muffin recipes I make, I used a teaspoon each of baking powder and baking soda. This recipe was okay--the muffins came out dry. If I were to make this again, I'd add a teaspoon of vanilla as well and maybe add some pureed peaches as well in place of some of the oil called for in this recipe and to make up for some of the liquid that's missing. For a half recipe, I got 12 muffins that were on the small side. I baked mine at 350 and they were done a just under 20 minutes.

text:
I used 3 cups of chopped peaches and the muffins turned out very tasty, moist and peachy.  6 very large peaches gave me the 3 cups.  I also used almost double the cinnamon, 1/2 cup olive oil, 3/4 cup applesauce, 1 cup whole wheat flour and 2 cups AP and baked them for only 20 minutes.  My peaches were slightly bitter so I didn't adjust the sugar at all and they turned out perfect that way.  It made 24 total regular sized muffins.  To get the skins off, I use the trick of putting the peaches in boiling water for 1 minute which also makes them slice & chop very easily.

text:
These were REALLY good, but did need that bit of milk as others suggested.  The key to "fluffy" is the amount of air you have in your batter.  Which means, do not "beat" your batter.  Using a fork, fold your batter gently 4-5 times, then turn and scrape the side of your bowl and fold 4-5 times more.  Continue until it is just moist.  STOP!  You are done.  Now add in any fruits you wish to use and JUST fold in enough to seperate the fruit and gently put into your pan.    I decided to put this batter into a 12" decorated bundt pan and it turned out wonderfully!  Took about 90 minutes though. (start checking at 75 min).  I also sprinkled a butter/brown sugar/flour/oatmeal in the bottom of the pan which added a little crispy to the top.  MMMM good!  For colour, I added 1 cup of blueberries to.  This was great and I will definetely make in the form of muffins to!

Delicious! My husband (semi-picky breakfast eater) wasn't too excited when I told him what I was making, but then ate half a dozen by himself. I didn't need any extra liquid since my peaches were very ripe and juicy. I don't know where 16 muffins came from...I got almost 3 dozen out of this recipe. I would definitely use paper liners, too. Since the recipe made so many, I didn't have enough, and the ones I baked without the liners stuck to the pan quite a bit...UPDATE: I just got some more paper liners, and made these again with a couple of changes. 1 cup packed brown sugar instead of 2 cups white, and replaced 1 cup of the oil with applesauce. They are just as yummy, and healthier, too! I'll make them like this from now on.

text:
Giving this a 5 star rating even though I made changes.  The changes were not because of the recipe, but due to lack of ingredients needed. Because of other reviews, I scaled the recipe down to 8 (1/2 recipe) and still made 12 muffins.  This is going to sound crazy...but the muffins came out AWESOME!  I substituted the oil with melted butter (equal measure). I used cornstarch in place of the eggs (2 Tbsp per egg). I used a 15 oz. can of Lite peaches in pear juice in place of the fresh peaches and I did add some of the juice since the mixture was dry (I didn't measure, just poured). I also subbed 1/2 of the sugar with brown sugar. The muffins came out awesome!  Some type of topping would be good but not needed. Definitely a "keeper". Thanks for sharing!

I followed this recipe exactly except for adding a teaspoon of vanilla and I was 1/2 a cup of peaches short. I added a tablespoon of sugar to my peaches as well and it made a nice syrup.

The batter was EXTREMELY thick, like a cookie dough. I thought I had done something wrong but I persevered. I added the peaches and it loosened up a little, but not that much.

I was tired and ready to go to bed so I just spooned them into the muffin pan.

They looked wonderful when they came out of the oven and when they had cooled down enough to eat.....

WOW! They taste SOOOOOOO good! (Especially after the spiced peach oatmeal muffin fiasco. DON'T waste your fresh peaches on that!)

But back to the peach muffins......It doesn't taste like a peach cobbler, to be sure. It tastes more like a cookie! Reminds me of snickerdoodles. Then when you get a bit of peach with it, it's like a party in your mouth!

The only change I would make is to add a cup of peaches to the 1/2 cup I was short. 

My daughter wants me to add that it's so sweet it makes your taste buds go wild.

This is a recipe I will definitely make again.

text:
These are great! However, like someone else's stated review...I just cannot follow a recipe all the way through. I made some modifications because both me and husband are diabetic. 

I took some suggestions from the other reviews and really tweaked some ingredients to suit us. 

I used 2 cups white flour and 1 cup whole wheat flour. Used 1 cup sugarless applesauce and 1/4 cup oil. 1 cup Splenda and 1/2 cup Splenda Brown Sugar. 

Added 1 cup chopped Mutsu apple (because I like the crunch of it), 1/2 cup dried cranberries, 1/2 cup chopped walnuts, 1 teaspoon baking powder and 1/2 cup fat free sour cream. Some of these are suggested by other reviewers and that was very helpful to me.

I did coat all the fruit and the walnuts with the combined flours, as someone else suggested. 

I ended up with 24 cupcake sized muffins and 12 mini muffins.

BTW my husband is eating them as I type this - but the real test will be our neighbor down the road. He's the muffin man in these parts! He'll either give me a two thumbs up, or a two thumbs down! I'm pretty sure I'll get them up tho'! :)

Yummy! These were delicious. I made some substitutions. I used 1 3/4 C lightly packed brown sugar in place of the white. I used 2 tins of peaches in natural fruit juice, drained. I used the drained liquid in the wet ingredients in place of 3/4C of the oil. Finally, I sprinkled some raw sugar on the tops before baking. This recipe made 18 regular muffins and 1 slightly flat (but delicious) cake. My husband loved these and was thrilled they were so light. Definitely a make again recipe.

text:
We live next to a peach orchard and pick peaches once a year, usually about 50 pounds or so.  I found this recipe years ago and have made it every year.  I don't make the muffins, but the bread.  This is a very good recipe.  The bread freezes very well, and is wonderful for breakfast with a hot cup of coffee.  At first I was a little hesitant about trying this recipe because of all the vegetable oil that it calls for for, but found that the oil is what makes it so moist.  This is a recipe I will continue to make through the years.

My husband and I enjoyed these muffins. I tweaked the recipe a little in an attempt to make them a bit healthier. I used 2c regular and 1c whole wheat flour, substituted applesauce for half of the oil, and decreased the sugar to about 1.5c. I also added a splash of milk since the batter was a little stiff. text:
These are, hands down, the best muffins I've ever had. They were not dry at all, not too sweet, but extremely flavorful. I did not find the need to top it with butter-or anything for that matter!  I did make a few changes. I added 1/4 tsp of orange extract, and added a handful of blueberries. I also was a tad bit of afraid of using 1 whole tablespoon of cinnamon, so I used 1 tsp. When I tried the muffin, that seemed enough to me.  Also, these were definitely done at 22 minutes (in my oven). Also, I don't know what pans you guys are using, but the batter I had made just one short of two dozen regular sized muffins.   I also found that five small peaches equaled to the needed 2 cups of chopped peaches (in case that helps anybody out :) ).  This is a fantastic, delicious, healthy, and very fast recipe. Thanks FBGMOMOF4!!!

text:
Oh, these are good. I didn't have quite enough peaches, so I made a half batch. Out of a desire to make the recipe a little more interesting, I added a splash of vanilla and swapped a little less than half the white sugar with brown, as well as sprinkling the top with a little extra brown sugar for a more interesting texture. My only problem with this recipe is that the muffin itself is a bit bland, when compared to the delectable, soft peach bits within. I'm planning on making these again, but I'll replace a quarter cup of oil with one pureed or crushed peach. This would also help make them moister - they already are, but more couldn't hurt.  I would also advise you not to worry if the batter seems very thick before you fold in the peaches - their juice will take care of that.

text:
This could have been a five star recipe, but I made it AS IS (I always do the first time, if I intend to rate it), and it was only okay. The high sugar content caused them to almost burn at 400. I turned it down to 325 to finish cooking the center and just salvaged them. They're good, but a bit bland, overly sweet, quite greasy, and very dense. Next time, I will increase the moisture so they get a better rise (some milk, perhaps), use only one cup of brown sugar, add way more fruit (some raspberries or cranberries would be great), a touch of vanilla, and less oil (or applesauce instead of half the oil). These have potential!

text:
These muffins were delicious . I edited the servings to 12 but still ended up with 16 muffins.  I made the following revisions to the adjusted recipe: used 2 1/2 c flour, 2 tsp cinnamon, nearly 3/4 c of canola oil, 4oz cup of unsweetened applesauce, 2 eggs, 2 cups of peaches (could have used more though), 1/2 c white sugar/Splenda and 1/2 c light brown sugar and I added 1/4 c of whole milk.  I used a 1/4 c scoop to fill the muffin cups to about 1/4inch from top.  And I topped them off with a mixture of 2 Tbsp of white and brown sugar, 2-3 Tbsp of chopped walnuts and @ 1/2 tsp of cinnamon. I baked them at 350 for around 15 min and they were perfect.  The only thing I need to figure out is how to disburse the peaches evenly through batter.  My entire family enjoyed even my 1 year old twins and my almost 4 year who said they were delicious!!!

Great way to use up peaches. I've made this several times, always with healthy changes and subs. I change the servings to 12, using 1 c AP flour, 1 c WW flour, and 1/8 c each ground flaxseed and wheat germ. I also sub Splenda blends (1/2 white, 1/2 brown) for the sugars, and 3/4 c natural applesauce and 1 6-oz ff peach yogurt for the oil. I like to throw in cinnamon and vanilla as well. Always very moist. I usually make mini-muffins baked @ 375 for 20 min.

Very good, tastes like peach cobbler! I used 1c whole wheat pastry flour and 2c bread flour. I too, as advised by other reviewers, added maybe 1/3c milk to the batter and a tsp of vanilla. I made THE BEST streusel topping in my food processor: 1/4c (leftover) candied pecans, 1/4c quick cook oats, 1T whole wheat flour, 1tsp cinnamon, 4T cold butter all pulsed until crumbly. I sprinkled this on top before baking a little over 20 minutes. I got 30 regular size muffins and used 5 good-sized pretty soft peaches. Thanks, will definitely make again!

text:
A+ recipe! Delish (with some modifications): only use fresh, ripe peaches. I used approx 10 leftover ripe peaches (small to medium sized)- did not peel, no need to because once cooked you cannot tell no difference. Chopped roughly. Only use 3/4 cups of veg oil (1.25 cups is a bit excessive for just muffin consumption). Add 1 tb of nutmeg (or more if you wish for taste). Used only white sugar and worked fine- no difference to brown sugar, unless you want to make some sort of topping. Cook at 400 degrees for 20-22 mins as per instructions. Note: this will make approx 16-18 large muffins, dependent upon how to distribute them. MUST spray muffin pan with Pam spray or something along those lines- if not, will stick to no avail. Enjoy! This recipe is amazing- fresh fruit taste with a hint of sweetness and nutmeg/cinnamon. Ate two immediately out of the oven and rest will probably be gone by tomorrow by family! :-)

A 5 stars for peach-y muffins! I used 5 very RIPE peaches. I blanched them in boiling water for 1 minute to get the skin off of the peaches. As I was chopping them up all the juices were coming out so I added as much as I could to the batter. I had about 2 1/2 cups of chopped peaches. I also used 1 1/4 cup of applesauce in place of the veg oil. This was the only adjustment I made to the recipe. The batter will be thick but when you add the chopped peaches along with its juices it will make for a nice consistency. The baking time was approximate. The were lovely pieces of peaches all over the muffins including the rounded muffin top - very pretty. The muffins were moist, light and refreshing. I smelled and tasted nothing but peaches. nice! Using only fresh ripe peaches with its juices made for a wonderful treat. I actually yielded 36 servings using regular cupcake muffin tins. I didn't have a texas size muffin baking pan. My only small criticism would be that it was kind of hard to get the paper liner off around the muffin. Other than that everything was fine.  Next time I may bake loaves 2 instead. Thank you FBGMOMOF4 for sharing this wonderful muffin.

I read the other reviews and modified this as follows for a wonderful, moist muffin (18): used 1/3 whole wheat flour (3/4 C + 2T = 1 C white--though an entire cup would not have hurt the results), 1/2 T cinn., 1/2 tsp corriander, 1/2 tsp salt, 1/2 C oil, >1/2 C pureed peaches + 1/2 tsp orange extract, 1 C Splenda, 1/2 C Spenda brown sugar, 3 C peaches, and 3/4 C walnuts. Cooking time was about 22 minutes. Yum!

I made this recipe into breads, and it was okay.  I actually doubled the recipe to make 4 breads, and because the peaches were so ripe, I cut back to oil to only 2 cups instead of 2-1/2.  The breads cooked fine and were extremely moist.  The only flaw in this recipe is that it wasn't overly flavorful.  With peaches having a mild flavor addition to the recipe, I felt it needed a boost somewhere, possibly in the spice area.  I should have followed some of the other reviewers and added to it.  I will probably use this recipe again, but use the bread slices as a base for an ice cream dessert, or for a fruit shortcake.

These were so good.  I made several changes to use up what I had on hand and make these a slightly healthier.   I added 1 c. mango/peach flavored applesauce (mainly because my son refuses to eat flavored applesauce :) and a 1/4 c. oil to replace the 1 1/4 c. of oil.  I thought that was just too much oil.   I also put 3/4 c. brown sugar, 3/4 c. white sugar to replace the 2 c. white sugar.  I added 1 t. vanilla (just because I love vanilla in just about everything).  I also added 1/4 t. nutmeg and 1/2 t. pumpkin pie spice. I only baked them for 20 minutes and might have still overcooked them.  They still turned out great.  Moist and very flavorful.  Thanks for this great, easily adaptable recipe!

text:
WAY too oily.  I should have gone with my instinct and cut way back on the amount of oil called for, and added yogurt or extra eggs for some of the liquid, but I gave the recipe a try as is, and I regret it. Not that the muffins tasted bad; they didn't, but they were very oily. They tasted like cookies to me, rather than muffins, and didn't have enough peach flavor, but everyone liked them. Next time I will cut back on the cinnamon also, which I think added to the cookie flavor. Oh, and I also had a problem with the recipe making more muffins than it said.  You could cut the recipe in half and still get a dozen decent-sized muffins.

text:
I cut the recipe in half and baked mine in a loaf container, using 3 large peaches that I chopped up, and subbing applesauce for half the required oil. As as result, I'm sure, of using applesauce and not measuring my super juicy peaches, I have juicy pockets around my peach chunks (which are rather large.) But--still delicious. I'll just heat the slices up when I serve them and dollop with whipped cream or ice cream, like a peach pie, but without the mess :) As far as flavor goes, it tastes like apple bread with peaches instead of apples. My peaches weren't nearly flavorful enough. I think I probably won't make peach bread or muffins again--I really prefer the apple version of this sort of thing, so I'll probably find other things to do with peaches!

text:
These muffins are yummy and great for that "quick on the go" breakfast or handing to the kids as they go out the door for school. I did make a few changes... first change (which I used on advice from another reviewer) instead of the 1 1/4 cups veg oil I used 1 cup cinnamon spiced applesauce and 1/4 cup veg oil, second change instead of the 2 cups sugar I used 2 cups Splenda (I'm diabetic) and third change was that I used 3 cups chopped fresh peaches instead of the 2. I also made 24 muffins instead of the 16 and baked them for 16 minutes. Since I made my muffins a little smaller there aren't as many calories per muffin (trying to watch my calorie intake). There's about 175 calories, 3 grams of fat and 31 grams of carbohydrate per muffin. Definitely a recipe I will make again! Thanks for sharing!

These were delicious! I cut the recipe in half and it still made 15 muffins.

Here is what I changedto make healthier: I did 1/4c applesauce and 1/4c olive oil instead of the vegetable oil. I used 2 eggs so I wouldn't waste half an egg. I also reduced sugar to half a cup and used coconut sugar in place of white. Pleasantly surprised with how tasty and moist these were! Definitely a keeper!

text:
Its awesome to come back and see what others think of your recipe and their changes. In the original recipe, I did use peaches that were extremely ripe, hence my hurry to use them.  They definitely had plenty of juice to add to the batter. ?? I posted this recipe before I even thought about healthy, now Im quite a bit more aware...older! I use applesauce for oil and often use maple syrup/agave/brown sugar for sugar. Sometimes I just use my ninja and pulse the peaches to get them distributed throughout...and I ALWAYS add pecans to them if my boys arent eating them (crazy kids dont like nuts!) I also use this recipe with strawberries and blackberries that are extremely ripe.  Its just the last step for my fresh fruit before its too far gone for anything. The best thing about baking is, contrary to what most think, if you have a general knowledge of baking, you can pretty much wing it.  Most things I do now are not measured and are using up things I have on hand...most turn out great (some, thank goodness only few, fail)

This recipe made 15 cupcakes, the leftover batter I poured in a loaf pan where it made a very short loaf.

I made these last year. We liked them but my kids didn't care for the chunks of peaches.

text:
Delicious! Obviously, like everyone else here I have tweaked it a little, due to the assortment of available ingredients at home, and simply, my urge to add something a little extra. Instead of veg. oil I have used half margarine and half grapeseed oil. Instead of white sugar I used brown. Here is what I added that made these muffins simply amazing: a tbsp of each - pumpkin seeds, dried cranberry and hemp seeds. Tablespoon of vanilla extract really made a huge difference.  This recipe calls for 400 degree oven temperature, which I personally wouldn't recommend to everyone, due to the fact that all ovens are different. If I baked at 400 in my oven, my muffins would come out burnt on the outside and wet on the inside (speaking from experience). So my oven did really well with 355 and I baked muffins for 30 min. They came out perfect! Will do it again!

The kids loved them, the mom loved them, my husbanf even loved them and asked me to make some for us.  fabulous great tasting recipe!

I made the original recipe except for one change made out of necessity:  adding some liquid.  When mixing the batter prior to folding in the peaches, the batter formed a ball - like bread dough. Also cut down on the sugar as they were very sweet to my tastebuds.

city:

text:
I made this once, tweaking based on other reviews.  And though it was very good, we still felt that it needed a more peachy flavor and a little something else.  I just finished making them a second time and think I've figured it out.  I used 1 Cup Whole Wheat Flour and 2 Cups unbleached AP flour.  Instead of all oil, I used 1.5 cups pureed peaches, sprinkled with some raw sugar (from 3 small peaches) and 1/2 Cup melted coconut oil. I added 1 tsp vanilla, and used only 1 tsp cinnamon.  I used only 1 Cup of raw sugar, and 2 large peaches yielded the 2 cups diced (Vidalia Chop Wizard works beautifully for this), which I also sprinkled with sugar.  I don't peel the peaches for either puree or diced.  What really made these stand out was that I added a cinnamon crumb topping: 1/3 Cup Sugar, 1/2 Cup Flour, 1.5 tsp Cinnamon and 1/4 Cup room temp. Butter (use pastry cutter, fork, or fingers until crumbly) - a heaping spoonful on each muffin before baking.  They were perfect after 22 minutes: moist, just sweet enough, and actually peachy tasting!  This made 32 full sized muffins, and with the changes I would give it 5 stars.

Delicious, easy recipe!  I've made these twice so far. text:
First time I did this recipe in a loaf pan,I followed it to the letter. Batter was way too wet and it took ages to bake, and  I ended up burning the top besides. So on my next attempt. I reduced the oil to just 50ml, and made up for it by adding about 1/4 cup of milk and more peaches, which I pureed. Also reduced the sugar to 300g as in my opinion, the peaches were sweet enough. Other alterations were adding 1 teaspoon of mixed spice and chopped walnuts. Batter came out nicely thick and "spoony". This time I carefully kept an eye on the oven, and put foil over the top of the pan in the final 20 minutes of baking. Cake came out nicely browned and tasted great. Will probably do it again, adding perhaps coconut or sultanas for variety.

I thought this recipe was very good.  I like nutmeg, so I cut back the cinnamon and added some.  I also added the suggested 1/2 cup of milk, we live in high altitude, so more moisture is needed.  My grandmother taught me to dissolve baking soda in fluid before placing it in the recipe to avoid its flavor when finished, so I put it in the milk.  Since my peaches lacked a little flavor last year, due to drought, I added a little peach flavoring.
